Free Talk

Words of Anguish

— Dujuan

Beloved compatriots. It would be good if Japanese warships did not come. But the arrival of Japanese warships is also within expectations, so there is no need to panic. Because before they take off their masks, they always claim to be protecting their overseas residents. Let's just listen and remain calm, and see what tricks they pull. However, the self-preserving people of Zhabei, upon hearing that Japanese warships had entered the Wusongkou, and lightly believing some unconscious rumors, had already begun to flee in droves. In fact, they had not even seen a shadow of Japanese soldiers. Why the rush? To make the Japanese laugh at our cowardice. If the country truly falls, then no matter where you flee to, you will still be a subjugated people. What is there to cherish about your life and property?

Conversations Without Removing Garden Grass Studio

The Three-Character Classic of Love

Before a person is born, the God of Love gives him or her a cup of love dew and says: "Take this cup of love dew and preserve it well. You can only drink it with the one you love the most!" This is Venus's command, and not a single word can be disobeyed. See how clear the words "only" and "most" are! If you only drink with the one you love the most, then the love dew is as sweet as honey; if you give it to anyone, it will turn into vinegar, into poison. Now, young people find love fascinating. I do not object. However, many young people treat lovers like Han Xin commanding soldiers: the more the better. They spend all day lingering in vinegar jars, cesspools, and poisonous gas chambers, forgetting their country, their studies, their careers, and their lives, ruining their reputations and regretting it too late. Last year, when Huang Baiying was forced to take poison by her lover, I wrote a Three-Character Classic to advise my young friends. Now I want to offer it to the young people of the whole country: "Happiness lies only in exclusive love!" The Three-Character Classic I wrote is: "Love's wine, sweet and bitter. Two people drink, it is nectar. Three people drink, it is sour like vinegar. If you drink it casually, it is poison among poisons." I wrote this Three-Character Classic, everyone must read it thoroughly!"

A Page of Tragic History of Japan's Annexation of Korea

— Zizai

The brutality of Japan's actions is arousing anger around the world. However, if we review the heartbreaking history of July 18th of the gengxu year, when Japan forcibly occupied Korea, we must awaken and contemplate. Since the conclusion of the Treaty of Shimonoseki, the situation in Korea suddenly changed. Those with insight knew that this land was no longer to be enjoyed by the Li family. However, the Korean Emperor, deceived by Japan's sweet words and hidden daggers, was encouraged to seek independence, thinking it would be the basis for a secure foundation and the eternal imperial legacy of his descendants. To confirm this, he even added honorific titles to himself, saying: "Heavenly Fortune Initiates the Ultimate, Promoting Ethics, Correcting Sacredness, Radiating Righteousness, Manifesting Merit, Great Virtue, Yao-like Sublimity, Shun-like Magnificence, Yu-like Planning, Tang-like Reverence, Responding to Destiny, Governing Principles, Achieving Transformation, Divine Fierceness, Majestic Achievements, Great Enterprise, Initiating the Foundation, Proclaiming and Experiencing the Operation of Qian, Establishing the Stability of Kun, Heroic Brilliance, Great Rest, Grand Emperor." It was as long as forty-nine characters, truly like a fish in a pot, unaware of its impending doom. On the day that Japan forcibly occupied Korea, an Imperial Council was convened. On this day, Korean Prime Minister Lee Wan-yong, Minister of Agriculture and Commerce Cho, Minister of Interior Park, representatives of the Imperial family, Prince Heung Lee Jae-myeon, Chairman of the Central Council Kim, and Japanese officials all gathered at the Injeongjeon Hall. Suddenly, the Korean Emperor, accompanied by attendant Yin and section chief Gao Lishi, appeared. The Korean traitor Lee Wan-yong stepped forward and reported: "Your Majesty, I observe the general trends of the world and the current state of Korea. For the benefit of the Korean people, it would be best to offer the land of Korea to Japan and receive its eternal protection. For the past few days, the cabinet ministers have carefully deliberated and dare to request Your Majesty's approval." At this time, the Korean Emperor closed his eyes and frowned. After a long while, he said, "I understand what you have reported. Handle everything according to your judgment." After speaking, tears streamed down his face. Most of the civil and military officials in the hall, except for those who had been informed in advance, were saddened. Thus, the fate of Korea was exhausted. After Japan annexed Korea, it established the Governor-General's Office to govern. Righteous patriots gnashed their teeth and were heartbroken, lamenting the oppression of autocracy and mourning the demise of their homeland. Those who advocated resistance fell one after another, and created the Independence Movement of 1919. But due to their weak strength and lack of support, they suffered setbacks. However, their indomitable revolutionary spirit has not ceased to this day. Because the Chinese Revolution has not yet succeeded, it is difficult for the Korean people to be independent. There is no doubt about this. Alas, the vast future, the silent continent. Looking up to the Northeast, grief is overwhelming. When our people see the brutality of the Japanese and the tragic demise of Korea, and read this page of Korean history, can they not shed tears of sympathy and rise up to save the country? Otherwise, they will become successors to the Korean people.

The Cold Fragrance Pavilion, Where Atrocities Remain

— Zheng Yimei

The Cold Fragrance Pavilion is a famous scenic spot in Tiger Hill, Suzhou. Since coming to Shanghai, I have not visited it for many years. Looking back on past travels, it feels like another world. The pavilion stands halfway up the mountain, with a commanding view. It was built by the local elder generation, Mr. Jin Hewang, Mr. Wang Dingcheng, and others. Three hundred plum trees are planted around it, creating a cold fragrance, hence the name of the pavilion. In early spring, those who love Lin Bu gather there to enjoy the scenery. In the crisp autumn days, they also come together for fun. In the cool winds of summer and the bright snow of winter, many couples also come. Throughout the four seasons, it is never deserted. People also taste tea in the pavilion, looking at the peaks of Lingyan, Zhiqi, Shangfang, and the Lion Ridge. The trains of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway wind through the lush greenery. A bird's-eye view offers a unique charm. I still remember once, when I and other literary friends gathered at the Cold Fragrance Pavilion, Shi Jiqun saw the trains and exclaimed at the spectacle. He couldn't help but blurt out, "From afar, the train looks like a snake." Cheng Zhanlu thought it was a seven-character couplet, like a ditty. So he jokingly added, "From up close, the train looks like a bus. If it's neither far nor near, the head is like a bus and the tail is like a snake." We all clapped and laughed. Unexpectedly, a few days later, news came that Japanese soldiers had shot and killed our Chinese youth. The youth, Hu Zonghan, happened to come here to enjoy the scenery. Two or three Japanese soldiers, indulging in hunting, also visited the pavilion as tourists. Seeing Hu Zonghan wearing a military uniform, they intentionally insulted him. Zonghan responded with harsh words. The Japanese soldiers then shot and killed him. His body lay in the pavilion for several days. The injustice was never redressed. Now, the iron heels of the Japanese barbarians are trampling on our Chinese territory, harming our compatriots beyond counting. If Hu Zonghan's soul is aware, in the dark, rainy weather, he must be howling like a spirit on the hills and in the lofty pavilion.

Record of Suppressed Tears

— Lingxiu

The national crisis is severe. It is painful to think about. Yet the ten-mile foreign concessions are still immersed in extravagance and decadence. The hearts of the people are dead. What a sigh! The Ministry of Education recently issued an order requiring cinemas to select patriotic films in order to stimulate public sentiment. This should be followed by film companies. However, there are very few domestic films that can express patriotic sentiments. In recent years, only a few films by the Mingxing Film Company, such as "New Journey to the West," "Black-Clad Heroine," "Struggling Marriage," and "Good Boys," have been seen. It is hoped that domestic filmmakers will act with patriotic enthusiasm and produce more of these films to create the greatest force for artistic propaganda. The revival of the national spirit relies heavily on this. The Japanese are inherently cruel. Domestically, they vigorously promote military-national education. All non-war novels and films are prohibited. Universal's "All Quiet on the Western Front" was once transported to Japan, but could not be screened anywhere, resulting in huge losses for the filmmakers. As for the films they produce themselves, they spare no effort in promoting the samurai spirit. From this, we can see their ambition.

Among American films, there are many that express patriotic thought and national spirit, such as "The Scarlet Empress" and "The Little Minister," to name just a few. What I especially love is "Revenge," starring Lila Lee and Glenn Tryon, because it can inspire patriotic thought in a moving way, rather than merely using crude stimulation to excite people temporarily.

Recently, foreign films screened in Shanghai mostly depict softness and extravagance, promoting decadence and hedonism. Yet our people flock to them, and the influence is significant. I believe that during this national crisis, the best thing for Chinese people to do is to endure hardship and strive for self-improvement. Otherwise, at the very least, we should promote domestic films as a minimum expression of patriotism. As for comedies and dance films, we should absolutely not watch them.

I heard that the Mingxing Company has recently completed "Red Tears." The emotional expression in the film surpasses that of "The Orchid in the Valley" and "The Falling Plum Blossoms." It is so sad and moving that the audience will be unable to hold back their tears.

Records of Happenings in the Former Capital

— Temple of Heaven's Imperial Vault of Heaven

The Temple of Heaven covers a wider area than the Forbidden City. Within the temple walls, ancient trees intertwine, and lush grass spreads, making one almost feel as if they are in the countryside. The altars of the Ming Dynasty were originally built in the southern suburbs. However, during the Wanli era, alarms from the northern border arrived daily. Fearing a sudden invasion by strong bandits, an outer city wall was built to enclose the people. Within the walled area, motherwort grew naturally. People specifically gathered this plant to make motherwort extract, which was considered more effective than that produced elsewhere. It was said in the past that the Imperial Ancestral Temple uniquely produced gray cranes that nested in pine and cypress trees, which, along with the grasses of the Temple of Heaven, were considered sacred products. The altar is constructed in three tiers, with white stone railings and steps. The height, width, and circumference all have fixed dimensions. North of the altar is the Imperial Vault of Heaven, a place prepared for conducting ceremonies in case of rain. North of the Imperial Vault of Heaven is the Hall of Prayer for Good Harvests, both with double-eaved roofs, resplendent in gold and green. European visitors to Beiping particularly marveled at the exquisite beauty of the Imperial Vault of Heaven. This is because the roof is extremely heavy, and the pillars are widely spaced. The even distribution of weight demonstrates unique ingenuity, representing the highest level of Eastern architectural art. Palaces and temples invariably adopt rectangular shapes, but the Imperial Vault of Heaven is circular, truly a masterpiece.

At the hour of Yin (3-5 AM) on the 24th day of the eighth month of the year Ji Chou in the Guangxu reign, thunder and lightning raged, and heavy rain poured down. Suddenly, the plaque of the Hall of Prayer for Good Harvests caught fire, which then spread. By the hour of Wei (1-3 PM), smoke and flames emerged from the lattice windows of the hall, igniting the beams and pillars. The blaze shone like a rainbow spanning the sky. Thereupon, the Commander of the Infantry issued command arrows and dispatched troops to rush to the rescue. However, because the hall was too tall, the water could not reach the flames. Eventually, the great hall with its eighty-one pillars was completely reduced to ashes. The fragrance permeated everywhere, reaching the main streets, because the hall's materials were all Phoebe nanmu, and the spirit tablets were sandalwood. Even the Han white jade on the steps (white stone produced in the Western Hills, with a quality like precious jade; many palace railings and staircases were made of this material, called Han white jade) was shattered. It was truly a strange disaster. Normally, palace fires are blamed on the custodians. However, it seemed that there was nothing to steal from the Hall of Prayer for Good Harvests. It is unknown how the fire started. After the incident, reconstruction was undertaken. The officials of the Ministry of Works thoroughly examined the regulations but found no record of its exact dimensions. Fortunately, an old craftsman was found who had participated in past repairs and vaguely remembered its structure. After much deliberation and searching, the work was finally completed, it is said.

With tears in their voices, the people were furious about the national crisis and wanted to weep but had no tears to shed. Perhaps when "Shadow of Red Tears" is screened, it can be used as a tool to evoke tears. I write this with restrained tears, hoping that these melancholic "Red Tears" can be transformed into patriotic tears of fervor.

Notes on Tea Tasting and Inkpad Appreciation

— Sun Choucheng

Mr. Dou Xia Yizi has an addiction to Lu Yu’s “The Classic of Tea” and is skilled at making inkpad. He uses the alias Ziyi and resides in the Xiyin Study in Ruikang Lane, North Nicheng Bridge, Shanghai. Yesterday, I received an invitation to taste tea and appreciate inkpad. He said a friend was coming from Hangzhou with Tiger Spring water, perfect for a pleasant drink. I went at three o'clock. Upon entering the room, I saw a couplet presented by the senior Zheng Xiaoxu, collected from Han Dynasty steles: "Closing the door to live quietly, a snow-white nature; writing diligently, orchids produce fragrance." His pure character was immediately apparent. He detailed the history of making inkpad, saying that he loved epigraphy in his youth and sought out rubbings from steles. He paid special attention to inkpad and visited various manufacturers, but none satisfied him. He then devoted himself to this craft. After twenty years and spending thousands of gold coins, he finally achieved success. He pointed out the items arranged on the table, classified into eight grades: Divine, Wonderful, High, Refined, Super, Excellent, Superior, and Good. He said that materials like cinnabar, coral, agate, and pearl are all hard in nature, making it difficult to grind them into fine powder. He has separately hired female workers to specialize in this task, coordinating the mixing and preparation. He believes that only he can do this job. Common inkpads use moxa floss, rush pith, willow catkins, and other materials. However, the divine-grade inkpad he makes uses lotus silk, combined with refined gold foil, beautiful split sand, and aged oil of several decades, which was not discovered by his predecessors. The color is as beautiful as a woman with a fair complexion, applying rouge. The inkpad is thin, the color is thick, and after printing, the stone is free of any fine residue. On paper, it is clean and flat. The longer it is stored, the more vibrant the color becomes. The selection of materials is special, hence its miraculous features. Using a stick to pick up the inkpad, it does not stick at all in the jar, and the pure white porcelain of the jar bottom can be seen. Only the most delicate lotus silk is used. The cost of materials and labor is unparalleled, making it a true treasure of the arts. Recently, due to a flood in his hometown, he is offering a 20% discount for three weeks, with all proceeds donated to flood relief. Soon, we moved to the guest hall to sit and taste tea. Besides me, there were also Mr. Zhu Dake and Mr. Gao Zhenying, as well as the former's two children. There were seven small teapots, eight small teacups, and one water bottle on the table. Mr. Xia personally washed the teapots and then placed a handful of tea leaves into one. First, he poured water into a bowl and tested its temperature on the outside of the bowl with his hand. Then, he poured the water into the teapot, frequently shaking it. He opened the lid to check the color and poured the tea into the cups to share. It had a unique flavor, as if we were in Longjing or Tiger Spring. The teas tasted that day included Mingqian Rain, Narcissus, and Plum Blossom, each with a different flavor. Finally, he also served pine nuts, walnuts, dried bamboo shoots, and lotus seeds as snacks, all made by Mr. Xia himself. I took my leave at five o'clock and wrote this as a record.

Fiction Society

The Pestle of Knocking Dreams (9)

— Cheng Zhanlu

The date of the provincial examination was approaching. "When acacia flowers turn yellow, the candidates are busy." Tao Chi was also one of these busy people. "Son!" When Tao Gongsheng called out this word, his tone contained twelve parts sincerity and expectation...

"Your writing has a manner of looking down from a height, striding forward vigorously. This is called 'original thought and original spirit!' If you don't pass, so be it; but if you pass, you have a good chance of excelling. You and Pei Shi both have great talent. It is a pity that Pei Shi misused his intelligence; this is also his own doing! You, on the other hand, stay on the proper path of the imperial examination, unlike Pei Shi, who went astray. Therefore, I recognize you as a promising lad. 'The day you pass the examination, your parents are not yet old...' Young scholar, strive on!"

Tao Chi, who was already confident, was further encouraged by his father's praise. He was even more determined to pluck the first branch of the cassia tree, not content with being second. He packed the necessary books for the three sessions into his examination basket, paying particular attention to the examination essays that Tao Gongsheng had revised for him.

He accidentally discovered a booklet with tiny, fly-head-sized characters in his desk drawer, which aroused his attention. He thought it was the crystallization of Tao Gongsheng's efforts, worthy of being collected in his examination basket. However, after reading only a few lines, he was ultimately disappointed! He casually wiped away the dust on the examination basket with the booklet and stuffed it into the wastepaper basket next to him, allowing the person collecting wastepaper to hold a cremation ceremony for it in the character-cherishing furnace! This desk was formerly the desk of his deceased friend Pei Shi; this booklet was also a manuscript left behind by his deceased friend Pei Shi. If it were solely written eight-legged essays, Tao Chi would have respected and preserved the relics of his deceased friend. However, upon opening it, it turned out to be what Old Man Pei and general public opinion considered useless and even harmful—descriptions of strange and ingenious crafts.

The few lines that Tao Chi saw and immediately discarded were Pei Shi's creations for playthings. The booklet said: "A plaything, although a toy, contains genuine principles; since play arises from principle, a gentleman should not abandon play altogether. The completed creations include automated plays with music, complete with everything, operating naturally without human effort. There is a lantern district: a small house is made, with several lamps suspended inside. People entering it feel as if they are entering a thoroughfare; the human smoke is dense, the lights are continuous, with a view of several miles. There is a self-propelled fan for dispelling heat: it can shake and create a breeze in the entire room without human effort. The above are all completed; I am drawing pictures and writing explanations for them..."

Youth Forum

Silence

— Xu Daitu

What a magnificent and grand auditorium, yet filled with solemn sadness and tense atmosphere. The people in the entire hall were standing silently at attention, bowing their heads in silent respect to the portrait of the Father of the Nation. Everyone held their breath, and the entire universe seemed desolate and still. Although they were silently mourning, in their minds and ears, they seemed to hear the rumbling of gunfire from the northeast.

Although they were silent, their blood was not cold but boiling. Everyone vowed to save the endangered motherland, and everyone was willing to fight the enemy with their lives. How could they allow the sacred and beloved Chinese people to be slaughtered?

How can we allow them to sleep soundly beside our bed? What are the Kellogg-Briand Pact and the League of Nations if not masks of the strong countries and painted cakes for the weak? The weak have never benefited from them, and the strong have never slightly restrained their ambitions. The survival of the fittest in the theory of evolution is not wrong. How can relying on others bring any benefit? If you want to survive in this world, you must strive to resist foreign aggression and seek a way to live. As long as we are united, how difficult is it to defeat the enemy completely? As long as we persevere to the end, how difficult is it to take the enemy's life? A true man dying on the battlefield, his body wrapped in horsehide, has fulfilled his national duty and his ambitions as a man. Moreover, at this time, it is a critical moment for our great Chinese nation. Moreover, we should take this opportunity to wipe out the past national humiliation of the Republic of China. Dr. Sun Yat-sen on the wall also dedicated his life for the country and the nation. We should live up to the Father of the Nation's earnest exhortations and expectations. We should strive to fight for the survival of our nation. Although the time of silence does not need to be long, that firm determination to strive and fight hard has been even more deeply etched in everyone's heart.

Class Meeting

— Benwu Shan

In the morning, the bell for the first class broke the calm air. Students, some carrying large stacks of books, came out of the dormitory, others came out of the reading room, talking as they slowly walked into the classroom. "Oh, cold-blooded animals, you can do your arithmetic problems so calmly...Heh, you really seem to be obsessed with arithmetic!"

"Don't calculate so obliviously. Now is not the time to calculate...and, think about it, what have you calculated anyway? This major incident of Japan forcibly occupying our South Manchuria, did you calculate that?" Mu Heyu came out of the reading room, walked into the classroom, and seeing his classmates sitting together quietly, seemingly very interested in calculating, couldn't help but jokingly say to them. "Cold-blooded animals, you're well-informed...We spent our entire evening class time last night discussing how to express our attitude toward Japan's forcible occupation of South Manchuria. Today, after all the students arrive, do you know what we're going to do?" Yu said triumphantly and mockingly, while stuffing his arithmetic textbook, exercise book, and other things into the drawer. "We're going to hold a class meeting to discuss the matter of Japan's invasion of our territory," class leader Li, who was also the chairman of the meeting, said seriously to Mu Heyu.

After a while, all the students in the class arrived. Chairman Li walked onto the podium with an "ah" sound, cleared his throat, and announced the official start of the meeting. Then, he asked us what method we should use to express our attitude towards Japan.

Before some students could think of an answer to the chairman's question, the arithmetic teacher for the first class began to appear hesitant at the classroom door.

"Oh, Mr. Wang, we are very sorry. Please lend us a few minutes to hold a class meeting. After we finish the meeting, we'll resume class," Chairman Li said as he welcomed the arithmetic teacher, who was hesitating outside the classroom, inside, in a seemingly respectful and solemn manner.

"Oh, hold a class meeting...Oh, it's not right to ask me to 'lend you a few minutes.' That's your time, not my time. And it's even more wrong to say 'we are very sorry,' because..." The arithmetic teacher's words could be said to be very complaining, but because his attitude when speaking was not serious but humorous, and the expression on his face was not one of unhappiness but of sympathetic sighs, the students did not mind at all and instead burst into laughter, interrupting the arithmetic teacher's words.

"Our school is one of the best in Shanghai and holds a leading position among schools. Therefore, I think the way we express our attitude towards Japan should be more enthusiastic, and we should especially sacrifice more of our class time. So, I propose that we all sacrifice class time and go out into the streets outside the school to give speeches, to let the general public hear about the plight of our country and Japan's vicious ambitions." Mu first proposed. When he finished speaking and sat down, he glanced at the arithmetic teacher, who was also paying attention to her at that time.

Many students expressed their opposition, some saying, "Giving speeches in the streets will disrupt social order." Some said, "Women's voices are relatively soft, so they are not suitable for giving speeches in public places." Some said, "The principal, the director of academic affairs, and the director of student affairs will definitely not agree to us going out to give speeches. They shout enthusiastic slogans to us, but this is just for us to hear, not for us to put into practice." Some said, "..." Many, many dissenting opinions.

In this way, one item was proposed on one side, and one item was refuted on the other. Finally, Mr. Wang said, "If you continue to debate like this, this meeting will never end. Why don't you just be casual...Oh, not casual...Why don't you just write some slogans and paste them everywhere." The students listened to Mr. Wang's words, and then they suddenly clamored into one piece. Some said, "I wanted to say that, but Mr. Wang took the words right out of my mouth." Some said, "Just pasting some slogans seems too simple." Some said, "..." But these are not important, because this proposal was finally agreed upon by most of the students and established.

When Mr. Wang heard that we had adopted his proposal, he said triumphantly, "What a pity, I had thought of this proposal a long time ago. Otherwise, if I had said it earlier, wouldn't we be able to be in class at this time? But, although, now you should dismiss the meeting. The things you want to do, wait until after class...Oh, take out your books, I want to teach." Mr. Wang slowly searched for the page he had taught in the previous class, intending to continue teaching.

"Mr. Wang, you are too calculating with us. Don't you know that we are very willing to sacrifice our time, if it is necessary for us to sacrifice?"

"Oh, does everyone agree to grind ink, cut paper, and write slogans now?"

"Arithmetic teacher, anyway, it's our time, let us finish this matter before we teach."

"Oh, half an hour is not enough. Mr. Wang, go to the teacher's office to rest. In this kind of emergency, we really have no heart to attend class."

"Mr. Wang, help us think of some slogans, okay? Because you might be able to think of some kind of slogan that people won't easily forget when they see it."

"Ah, really, arithmetic teacher, you can really show your great skill and calculate!"

Many students who liked to make trouble, each said a sentence, with serious faces, pretending to be respectful, stood up and said to Mr. Wang.

"Alright, do whatever you like. You are originally sacrificing your time to do your patriotic actions." After Mr. Wang finished speaking, he coldly walked out of the classroom. At that time, other classes were in session, and everything was silent except for the voices of the teachers. "Tap...tap..." Very clearly, the sparse sound of Mr. Wang's leather shoes echoed slowly, as if sighing.

Before and After the Occupation of Shenyang

— Zhu Fujun

The daylight-like lights suddenly disappeared, and a faint green glow instantly appeared before our eyes.

The sound of the violin slowly echoed on the stage, like a dream. The temptation of color, the writhing of flesh, thunderous applause from the audience below the stage, dancers intoxicated, dancing stars graceful, the temptation of color, the writhing of flesh, thunderous applause from the audience below the stage, "Ah!" Suddenly, a stray bullet—a stray bullet quietly flew in through the glass window, and the struck dancer suddenly let out such a miserable cry.

In the midst of the miserable cry, he suddenly fell down. Everyone's faces turned pale. The lights suddenly brightened. Chaotic figures filled the dance hall. The lights suddenly brightened, followed by the mournful cries of women.

○　　○　　○

The refugee train was just starting to move its cars, fully loaded with people, people.

Cries, cries.

The train moved forward quickly. The sounds of gunfire, artillery, collapsing houses, and people gradually faded into the distance, further and further away. What remained was only the lonely sound of weeping on the train.

The train moved forward quickly. The sounds of gunfire, artillery, collapsing houses, and people gradually faded into the distance, further and further away. The strong young men jumped off the train, ready to sacrifice themselves.

○　　○　　○

Smoke filled the sky above Shenyang's city walls. The wind in Shenyang carried the furious cries and curses. Shenyang's arsenal was exploding. The tragic songs of the men resounded through the clouds.

"Forward, forward, forward! You barbarian dwarfs! You have sharp guns and cannons, you have boiling red blood, you have extraordinary arrogance, but here we have prepared courage and determination!"

○　　○　　○

Beside the strong young man who jumped off the train, a fierce Japanese soldier approached from afar. He walked toward him with a lewd smile. He rushed forward, seized the soldier's sword, and killed him.

He obtained this moment of joyful release of anger, but suddenly—

Suddenly, a bullet pierced his back. He turned around and saw three or four enemies behind him. He wanted to chase after them—but he fell to the ground. A faint sunlight shone over the earth, leaving an immortal mark on a corner outside Shenyang city.

Book Review

Twenty Years of Manchukuo and Mongolia Under Japanese Influence

Edited by: Chen Jing

Now, we are facing a national crisis, a critical moment for the survival of the nation. In recent days, the urgent news in the newspapers, the sorrowful and tragic cries, have shaken the Central Plains and the entire world. This time, Japan's invasion of the Northeast, the plundering of our land and property rights, the slaughter of our compatriots, the inhumanity of its iron heel, and its advance to probe key locations such as Qingdao, Tianjin, Beiping, Nanjing, and Shanghai, boasting and demonstrating, provoking challenges, intending to annex, this alarming and frightening scene, puts our country in a precarious situation.

However, people must first decay before others insult them. If we put our hearts into investigating the reasons for today's crisis, we cannot help but hate the fact that for twenty years, the Chinese people have paid too little attention to Manchuria and Mongolia. This negligence and misjudgment has gradually evolved into today's tragedy.

Therefore, the book "Twenty Years of Manchukuo and Mongolia Under Japanese Influence" is truly a clear and resounding bell in the middle of a deep sleep, simply and vividly revealing the ferocious and encroaching face and frightening situation of the Japanese empire before our eyes, giving the people a stark awakening, urging them to rise up quickly and take action. Manchuria and Mongolia are the focus of contention among the great powers in the "Far East Problem," and Japan regards the development of its survival relationship as even more critical. It represents everything with the "Manchuria-Mongolia Problem," clearly concentrating its aggression and obtaining special benefits from special relationships.

Japan's invasion of Manchuria and Mongolia is the implementation of its "continental policy" over the past twenty years, that is, in its colonial method of plundering raw materials and selling goods, it has promoted the final stage of its capitalism.

The motivation for compiling "Twenty Years of Manchukuo and Mongolia Under Japanese Influence" seems to be the association and impression forced out of the taste of "miso soup" poured over white rice, a mysterious food that the author, Mr. Chen Jing, encountered every day while living abroad. Let us look at a passage from his "Memories After Writing This Book":

"In the Dalian area of Liaodong Peninsula, our Chinese Eastern Three Provinces, Japanese factories produce more than 1 million catties of this thing. Japanese factories in Fengtian produce more than 1 million catties. Japanese factories in Gongzhuling along the South Manchurian Railway also produce more than 40,000 catties. Last year, more than 3 million catties were transported from Manchuria to Japan for consumption, worth more than tens of thousands of yuan. These 'miso' are made from a portion of the more than 4,000 shi of soybeans from Manchuria and Mongolia. These 4,000 shi of soybeans are cultivated from more than 40,000 mu of farmland in Manchuria and Mongolia by the countless sweat and blood of the people. Last year, more than 25 million catties of soybeans were transported from Manchuria to Japan. Some of these soybeans were also turned into 'miso.' Perhaps an extremely small portion of these 'miso' was eaten by me."

From tasting the flavor of "miso" to thinking about the situation of his homeland, he felt even more painfully that drops of fresh blood were being squeezed away by others. This is what the author finds most distressing, and this may already be a microcosm of the Manchuria-Mongolia policy in reality. The book analyzes Japan's deeply rooted colonial policy in Manchuria and Mongolia over the past twenty years, such as how many Japanese colonists there are in Manchuria and Mongolia, what methods they use to solve their colonial life, and what is Japan's immigration policy toward Korea, how many Koreans are there, what is their degree and nature, where do they immigrate to, what policy does Japan adopt toward them, how does it force them, how does it use them, secondly, how does Japan politically oppress Manchuria and Mongolia, how does it plunder them economically, how does it invest, how does it plunder raw materials and labor, how does it sell its surplus goods, how does it extract profits and currency, how does it engage in monopoly in the transportation industry, how does it engage in aggression in the cultural industry, and finally, to what extent will it develop its colonial policy, all of which are analyzed in this book. The book uses population as the object of study when looking at the number and nature of Japanese colonists in Manchuria and Mongolia, as well as their immigration methods and places of immigration. This is the outline of Japan's colonial policy, which is the general theory of this book. As for Manchuria and Mongolia, the various forms of Japanese oppression and aggression in the political, economic, transportation, and cultural fields are the functioning of Japan's colonial policy. This is moving from the outline to the strength, which is the special theory of this book.

Page 20

The general theory describes the overview of Japanese colonization of Manchuria and Mongolia and is divided into two chapters.

The first chapter explains the relationship between Japan's rapid population growth and its colonization of Manchuria and Mongolia. Since the Meiji Restoration, from 1870 (Meiji 3) to 1920, in 57 years, Japan's population rapidly increased from more than 33 million to more than 55.9 million, which is no longer comparable to the slow population growth rate before the industrial development from 600 years ago to 1868. Due to the rapid population growth and material panic, it then colonized our country's Eastern Three Provinces and Inner Mongolia to realize its policy of plundering land and capital. Its colonization methods are: first, directly colonizing Manchuria and Mongolia, which it has been advocating for twenty years with the slogan of 4 million Manchurian and Mongolian colonists. Looking at the tables of Japanese households and population in Manchuria and Mongolia in each year in the book, we know that the Japanese colonial population in Manchuria and Mongolia is increasing year by year, with leased territories and railway-affiliated areas as the concentration points, gradually infiltrating into the depths of Manchuria and Mongolia; second, indirectly colonizing Manchuria and Mongolia. Japan initially immigrated to Korea, and then forced Korean people to immigrate to Manchuria and Mongolia. The total number of indirect immigration from Koreans to Manchuria and Mongolia is more than five times the total number of Japanese in Manchuria and Mongolia. This is really a pungent policy of Japan, clearly expressing the ambition of Japanese imperialism.

The second chapter describes the relationship between Japan's entire colonial policy and its Manchuria-Mongolia colonial policy. Originally, Japan's colonial policy was realized in different ways based on three arguments: (1) the Greater Asia policy, which is to invade all of Asia from Manchuria and Mongolia, also known as the Northward Expansion Theory; (2) the Southward Expansion Theory, which is to colonize the South Sea Islands, Australia, and the vast Pacific coast of the Americas to build a new Japan; (3) the Secret Strategy of Universal Unification, which is to colonize everywhere in the world. However, the Southward Expansion Theory and the Secret Strategy of Universal Unification clash with the colonial strategies of European and American imperialism. As a result, it has suffered severe exclusion from the United States and British self-governing colonies, and there is no possibility of development. Therefore, Japan had to change its colonial argument and concentrate on attacking the Eastern Three Provinces and Inner Mongolia, that is, to realize the so-called Northward Expansion Theory.

Japan's form of colonizing Manchuria and Mongolia is the result of its competition with various imperialist countries for colonies and its aggression against weak foreign nations and oppression of weak domestic people. It treats Manchuria and Mongolia in the same way as it treats colonization and Korea. Its Ministry of Internal Affairs handles the reception, protection, supervision, and promotion of overseas immigration associations. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs handles subsidies for colonial travel expenses and publishes reports on colonial surveys. Its recent outline for revitalizing colonization, comprehensively speaking, includes: (1) cultivating and popularizing colonial thought; (2) emphasizing publications and publicity in Manchuria and Mongolia and the activities of organizing associations; (3) giving full play to the mutual production relationship and characteristics of various Japanese colonies; (4) using colonial policies to deal with the recent disputes among rural tenant farmers in Japan. The special theory explains the function of Japan's colonial policy toward Manchuria and Mongolia, which is entirely concentrated on unequal political forces and relies on the military to be the pioneers and supporters of such treaty expansion, or is constructed by colluding with warlords and politicians with money. China's most significant losses in these abnormal treaties: (1) Regarding land lease rights, administrative rights, and freedom of residence, etc.; (2) Regarding railway operations and loan rights, etc.; (3) Regarding mining and forest exploitation rights and company joint ventures, etc.; (4) Regarding tariff exemption rights or reduced special rights, etc. In short, the rights that Japan has obtained in Manchuria and Mongolia are all obtained through unequal treaties.

This chapter describes in detail (1) Japan's political efforts and its organization in Manchuria and Mongolia; (2) Japan's implementation of police power and special forms in Manchuria and Mongolia; (3) Japan's exploitation of taxes and miscellaneous levies in Manchuria and Mongolia; (4) The issues of the Japanese troops and their power deployed in Manchuria and Mongolia are all thoroughly explored and accompanied by various tables.

The first part recounts the function of Japan's economic aggression, which is due to the effect of unbalanced imports, and is divided into five chapters: The first chapter, on the plundering of raw materials, such as (1) the minerals of Manchuria and Mongolia; (2) the forests of Manchuria and Mongolia; (3) the animal husbandry of Manchuria and Mongolia; (4) the aquatic products of Manchuria and Mongolia; (5) the agricultural products of Manchuria and Mongolia. The second chapter, on investment in commerce and industry, such as (1) financial domination; (2) monetary monopoly; (3) trade monopoly; (4) commerce; (5) industry, etc. The third chapter, transportation, such as (1) railways; (2) shipping; (3) communications, etc. The fourth chapter, culture, such as (1) education; (2) religion; (3) the publishing industry, etc., are all based on statistics. After this is the epilogue.

I have given a brief introduction to this book as outlined above. I feel infinite thoughts in my heart. Although we hate Japan's atrocities in the Northeast and are working together to overcome the national crisis, we cannot help but be amazed by their organized and prepared work and spirit on weekdays. The materials in this book are very rich, and some of the illustrations and tables are not easy to find. I hope readers will pay special attention to them and keep the impressions after reading deeply in their minds as firm fuel for our spirit and intellect.

Youth Forum

Not Dead

— Huang Huanruo

{Comfort gained from publicity work}

The incident of the violent Japanese trampling on the Eastern Provinces is expanding day by day. Our territory is gradually being蚕食 by them, and large numbers of our compatriots are being slaughtered by them. This barbaric and cruel beastly behavior does not seem to be restrained by justice, nor can its conscience be revealed by non-resistance.

I, who have always advocated that studying hard is saving the country, can no longer calm my surging passion and surging emotions at this critical moment. It is true that under the cover of such numb and non-resistant people, it is no longer the time for us to study. Because the responsibility of saving the country can only be shouldered by us pure-hearted youths and the people. I have suddenly realized that I dare not put down my books, and I cannot move my body outside. Standing under the banner of reading without forgetting to save the country, I finally joined the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. As a member of the warrior, anger burns in my heart, and indignation inspires my chest. I can't help but shout out such awakening words under the shaking small flag, "Saving the country cannot passively wait for the enemy's conscience to be discovered, because beasts have no conscience. Saving the country cannot rely on the just aid of the great powers, because the world has obliterated justice. To save the endangered China from destruction, we can only rely on our own strength, our own courage. This is a good opportunity for us to serve the country."

Thousands of resolute and courageous young people lined up like long snakes on the school road, waiting spiritedly for the time of departure to come. Hardworking students have left the library, and delicate female students have also stepped out of the palace gate. All comfort and enjoyment will no longer haunt everyone's minds. The ferocious beastly face and brutal cruelty of the Japanese invaders seem to be unfolding before our eyes.

Our team was sent to the Wusong countryside to carry out propaganda. So we took the train to our destination, Wusong. Qiu held the small flag in front and led the way, because he was familiar with the geography of Wusong.

Walking out of Songzhen, a group of fifteen people walked excitedly along the rugged narrow path towards the village hidden in the greenery.

Beside a small lake, there was a green grassy beach, which was outside a village. We stopped here to discuss the outline of the propaganda, arranged the order of the speeches, and the fifteen of us simultaneously swore an oath on the responsibility of saving the country. Our oath was:

"From today onwards, we are determined to engage in the work of saving the country. We are not afraid of difficulties, we are not afraid of death. We are willing to sacrifice everything to go to the national crisis. We will eliminate selfish desires and eliminate the habit of relying on others. We should unite and work together to seek the country. If there is any behavior that violates the oath, it should be abandoned by the people, sworn by all members of the XX Propaganda Team of XX University, September 25, 20th year."

A few minutes later, we had dispersed throughout the village and began our propaganda work.

The impression of the Japanese people's brutality has been deeply rooted in the hearts of the entire nation since the May Fourth Movement. When we reported the motives for our speech, the farmers said in unison, "What, are the Easterners (commonly known as the Japanese as Easterners) bullying us Chinese again? Dwarf slaves, hateful dwarf slaves." Groups of farmers put down their work and listened quietly to our speeches.

Fang's speech was extremely impassioned, extremely sincere, and extremely indignant. The farmers listened to her moving speech and constantly whispered, "This female teacher is right. We should not buy Dongyang goods (Japanese goods). We should join the army. Damn it, if we don't kill the Dongyang people, we can no longer eat in peace."

"Female teacher, if the Japanese are so unreasonable and so fierce, why don't we go to war with them?" A farmer eagerly asked Fang. Many faces pressed close to her, as if waiting to solve this doubt. "We don't fully understand the government's intentions for this reason, but the biggest reason is probably that the armaments are too bad to fight against Japan. Now we are urging the government to prepare for war. If the Japanese soldiers refuse to withdraw, then it is expected that a war will eventually break out." "Damn it, waiting for the war, let's all rise up and fight the dwarfs to see who is stronger."

"Teacher, can we also join the army to fight the Dongyang people?" The voices were noisy, and the flames of ardent patriotism were blazing.

"Yes, the National Salvation Volunteer Army will be organized soon, which will welcome you to participate. If you are willing to sacrifice your lives to save the country, then you can sign up, join the military training, and when necessary, you will have to go to the front line and fight a life-and-death battle with the enemies."

When we first entered the village, what we saw was only an unusual calm. At a time when the national crisis was dire, we felt pity and deathly silence when we looked at the passionate and energetic people. It seemed that we vaguely felt the sorrow that people's hearts were dead and the country's affairs were hopeless. However, after our speech, the farmers' passionate blood, excited courage, and spiritual expression suddenly excited us. Although the superiors are numb and indifferent, the hearts of the people are still active, and the country's destiny should not be cut off. Two hours later, we left the lovely and promising farmers amidst a tragic farewell.

In addition, we found another village. Naturally, everything was generally the same as in the previous village. I couldn't help but sigh and say, "Only these simple farmers can save the country. Unfortunately, they have not been given sufficient education and cultivation, which has left them in intellectual hunger." The teammates all sympathized with my words, and popularizing mass education made us even more believe that it was one of the lasting methods of saving the country. On the way back, darkness enveloped the vast twilight. In the tension of the autumn wind, we finally suffered a heavy rain. Wet clothes pressed against our skin, which was very uncomfortable. But when I thought of the compatriots in the Eastern Provinces who had been swept by guns and artillery fire, I felt relieved.

"The days to come will be filled with artillery fire and bombs. What does this mere wind and rain count for?" Yan's cheongsam was soaked by the rain and clung tightly to her body. She stumbled through the mud and said heroically.

Propaganda and the Ah Q Era

— Jun Liang

When the news that the violent Japanese had advanced into the Eastern Three Provinces and forcibly occupied our territory reached our school from the newspapers, it was early morning and the sunlight was vaguely shining on the flagpole of the gymnasium in the northeast corner of the school. The students restrained their usual smiles, and their minds were filled with sad and resentful thoughts. The students' blood boiled.

The next morning, the playground was full of students. In the past, perhaps a游艺会 could have enticed so many people. The chairman announced, "If there are any students who do not attend today, we would rather not hold the meeting." Then there was a burst of applause. Finally, the meeting began.

Under the scorching sun, our speakers who wept and spoke

Page 22

and the students who listened attentively, their faces were red and their ears were burning hot.

After a few days of discussion and meetings, the result was to go out for publicity. The old articles from before, although old, might have some effect on the numb and indifferent Chinese people. We initially held this hope.

Our team was sent to a small town in the northeast of Shanghai. It was not far from the cultural center of Shanghai. When we arrived at our destination, we carried out propaganda, distributed leaflets, and gave speeches. The people were at the market near the small bridge late in the evening. We stood still. The village children first aroused curiosity. They wanted leaflets. The number of people gathered was not small. We started speaking. They were all furtive, as if afraid of us, with rare expressions of surprise on their faces.

"...The Japanese are now killing our compatriots," the speaker shouted loudly.

"Japanese..." An old man frowned and whispered something in the ear of a relatively young middle-aged man.

"Foreign executioners," the middle-aged man replied impatiently.

"Easterners! Dwarf slaves! We don't want to buy Dongyang goods!" The speaker raised his voice very high.

"Oh, Dongyang people," the old man and the middle-aged man both indicated that they understood.

"You can ask whatever you don't understand." When the speaker shot his gaze at the old man's face, he hurriedly turned around and left. The middle-aged man and many children and women were also silent. It was drizzling, and they gradually dispersed, and we also left.

When we arrived at a bustling market, we gave speeches in a more crowded place. The speaker was very sincere, and the listeners also looked elsewhere, nodding to indicate that they understood. Suddenly, a long-faced man said with a contemptuous expression, "The Dongyang people only know how to beat the Chinese, because our mouths can't move. To be honest, the Dongyang people have come here, and we two will fight one, tear them apart and eat them. What's the use of you talking?" After he said this, he stared at the sky, as if he really saw two people tearing one person apart and eating them. "What you said is true, but many people still don't know that the Dongyang people are killing us at the door."

"I understand very well... In fact, there are all kinds of foreign executioners in Shanghai, and they won't let the Dongyang people in. We can rest assured." He glanced around, thinking that this was his highest opinion.

Finally, we arrived at the town's public opinion representative place, the teahouse. It was almost full of tea drinkers. We started speaking at the table of an old man with a monk's head. The monk's head had a face full of horizontal flesh, and two rows of beards hung down from the corners of his mouth. While we were speaking, the monk's head kept lifting his thick lips, wanting to speak. Finally, we finished speaking, and he opened his mouth.

"We country people wear our own old cloth and eat yellow rice. Not to mention Dongyang goods, we don't even use Western goods." As he spoke, he looked at our clothes, as if saying, "Look at yourselves." We were speechless.

"You scold the Dongyang people, but we country people either have braids or shave our heads. Haha, combing Dongyang's head and scolding the Dongyang people." The monk's head touched his beard and smiled, revealing his waxy yellow teeth. Then everyone in the teahouse laughed.

It was raining again. Raindrops poured in from the northeast corner of the teahouse. The tea drinkers moved around one after another. We took advantage of the chaos, put on our raincoats, and left the teahouse.

In the gloomy twilight of the cold wind and rain, we walked out of this small town, and still seemed to hear harsh laughter.

The Ah Q era is not dead.
